The name corresponds to the Greek spelling&nbsp;<em>Iesous</em>, from which, through the Latin&nbsp;<em>Iesus</em>, comes the English spelling&nbsp;<a href=”http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jesus” target=”_blank” title=”Jesus”>Jesus</a>.<sup class=”m_335559167484459286m_-2462594541108499772gmail-m_-1644936308594193845gmail-m_-1425260696292380041m_-6606627327515452666m_6605744291038607384m_-1341156577359935856m_1143141077132377639m_5371528777137425371m_7312233276763737620gmail-m_-7699896603790004333gmail-m_2515164250424317772gmail-reference” id=”m_335559167484459286m_-2462594541108499772gmail-m_-1644936308594193845gmail-m_-1425260696292380041m_-6606627327515452666m_6605744291038607384m_-1341156577359935856m_1143141077132377639m_5371528777137425371m_7312233276763737620gmail-m_-7699896603790004333gmail-m_2515164250424317772gmail-cite_ref-1”><a href=”http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yeshua#cite_note-1” target=”_blank”>[1]</a></sup><sup class=”m_335559167484459286m_-2462594541108499772gmail-m_-1644936308594193845gmail-m_-1425260696292380041m_-6606627327515452666m_6605744291038607384m_-1341156577359935856m_1143141077132377639m_5371528777137425371m_7312233276763737620gmail-m_-7699896603790004333gmail-m_2515164250424317772gmail-reference” id=”m_335559167484459286m_-2462594541108499772gmail-m_-1644936308594193845gmail-m_-1425260696292380041m_-6606627327515452666m_6605744291038607384m_-1341156577359935856m_1143141077132377639m_5371528777137425371m_7312233276763737620gmail-m_-7699896603790004333gmail-m_2515164250424317772gmail-cite_ref-2”><a href=”http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yeshua#cite_note-2” target=”_blank”>[2]</a></sup></span><br /> <span style=’font-family: “times new roman” , serif; font-size: xx-small;’><br /></span><span style=’font-family: “times new roman” , serif; font-size: xx-small;’>The Hebrew spelling&nbsp;<em>Yeshua</em>&nbsp;(ישוע) appears in some later books of the Hebrew Bible. Once for&nbsp;<a href=”http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joshua” target=”_blank” title=”Joshua”>Joshua</a>&nbsp;the son of Nun, and 28 times for&nbsp;<a href=”http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joshua_the_High_Priest” target=”_blank” title=”Joshua the High Priest”>Joshua the High Priest</a>&nbsp;and (<a class=”m_335559167484459286m_-2462594541108499772gmail-m_-1644936308594193845gmail-m_-1425260696292380041m_-6606627327515452666m_6605744291038607384m_-1341156577359935856m_1143141077132377639m_5371528777137425371m_7312233276763737620gmail-m_-7699896603790004333gmail-m_2515164250424317772gmail-mw-redirect” href=”http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/KJV” target=”_blank” title=”KJV”>KJV</a>”Jeshua”) and other priests called Jeshua – although these same priests are also given the spelling Joshua in 11 further instances in the books of&nbsp;<a href=”http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Book_of_Haggai” target=”_blank” title=”Book of Haggai”>Haggai</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a href=”http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Book_of_Zechariah” target=”_blank” title=”Book of Zechariah”>Zechariah</a>. It differs from the usual Hebrew Bible spelling of&nbsp;<a href=”http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joshua” target=”_blank” title=”Joshua”>Joshua</a>&nbsp;(יְהוֹשֻׁעַ&nbsp;<em>y’hoshua<wbr></wbr>ʿ</em>), found 218 times in the Hebrew Bible, in the absence of the consonant&nbsp;<a href=”http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/He_(letter)” target=”_blank” title=”He (letter)”>he ה</a>&nbsp;and placement of the semivowel&nbsp;<a class=”m_335559167484459286m_-2462594541108499772gmail-m_-1644936308594193845gmail-m_-1425260696292380041m_-6606627327515452666m_6605744291038607384m_-1341156577359935856m_1143141077132377639m_5371528777137425371m_7312233276763737620gmail-m_-7699896603790004333gmail-m_2515164250424317772gmail-mw-redirect” href=”http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vav_(letter)” target=”_blank” title=”Vav (letter)”>vav</a>&nbsp;ו after, not before, the consonant&nbsp;<a href=”http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shin_(letter)” target=”_blank” title=”Shin (letter)”>shin ש</a>. It also differs from the Hebrew spelling&nbsp;<em><a href=”http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yeshu” target=”_blank” title=”Yeshu”>Yeshu</a></em>&nbsp;(ישו) which is found in&nbsp;<a href=”http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eliezer_Ben-Yehuda” target=”_blank” title=”Eliezer Ben-Yehuda”>Ben Yehuda</a>’s dictionary and used in most secular contexts in&nbsp;<a href=”http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Modern_Hebrew” target=”_blank” title=”Modern Hebrew”>Modern Hebrew</a>&nbsp;to refer to&nbsp;<a class=”m_335559167484459286m_-2462594541108499772gmail-m_-1644936308594193845gmail-m_-1425260696292380041m_-6606627327515452666m_6605744291038607384m_-1341156577359935856m_1143141077132377639m_5371528777137425371m_7312233276763737620gmail-m_-7699896603790004333gmail-m_2515164250424317772gmail-mw-redirect” href=”http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jesus_of_Nazareth” target=”_blank” title=”Jesus of Nazareth”>Jesus of Nazareth</a>, although the Hebrew spelling&nbsp;<em>Yeshua</em>&nbsp;(ישוע) is generally used in&nbsp;<a href=”http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bible_translations_into_Hebrew” target=”_blank” title=”Bible translations into Hebrew”>translations of the New Testament into Hebrew</a><sup class=”m_335559167484459286m_-2462594541108499772gmail-m_-1644936308594193845gmail-m_-1425260696292380041m_-6606627327515452666m_6605744291038607384m_-1341156577359935856m_1143141077132377639m_5371528777137425371m_7312233276763737620gmail-m_-7699896603790004333gmail-m_2515164250424317772gmail-reference” id=”m_335559167484459286m_-2462594541108499772gmail-m_-1644936308594193845gmail-m_-1425260696292380041m_-6606627327515452666m_6605744291038607384m_-1341156577359935856m_1143141077132377639m_5371528777137425371m_7312233276763737620gmail-m_-7699896603790004333gmail-m_2515164250424317772gmail-cite_ref-3”><a href=”http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yeshua#cite_note-3” target=”_blank”>[3]</a></sup>&nbsp;and used by Hebrew speaking Christians in Israel.
